**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Incident Debugging: Envoy Connection Pool Exhaustion

## Your Task

A production Envoy proxy is logging `upstream connect error or disconnect/reset before headers. reset reason: overflow`. Trace the error to its source in `envoyproxy/envoy`. Find: 1. The C++ source file that defines the `overflow` reset reason string. 2. The connection pool implementation files under `source/common/conn_pool/` or `source/common/http/` that trigger this overflow condition. 3. The configuration protobuf in `envoyproxy/data-plane-api` that controls `max_connections` and `max_pending_requests` circuit breaker thresholds.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive trace of the Envoy connection pool exhaustion error. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

### 1. **The "overflow" Reset Reason String**
Located in `source/common/http/utility.cc:1031`, the `resetReasonToString()` function maps `Http::StreamResetReason::Overflow` enum to the literal string `"overflow"` that appears in error logs.

### 2. **Where Overflow is Triggered**
In `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc`:
- **Lines 282-287**: When pending requests exceed `max_pending_requests` limit
- **Lines 175-179**: When active requests exceed `max_requests` limit

Both call `onPoolFailure()` with `ConnectionPool::PoolFailureReason::Overflow`.

### 3. **Circuit Breaker Configuration**
The protobuf definitions are in:
- **Envoy repo**: `api/envoy/config/cluster/v3/circuit_breaker.proto`
- **Data-plane-api repo**: `envoy/config/cluster/v3/circuit_breaker.proto` and `envoy/api/v2/cluster/circuit_breaker.proto`

Key fields controlling the limits:
- `max_connections` (default: 1024)
- `max_pending_requests` (default: 1024)  
- `max_requests` (default: 1024)

### 4. **Call Chain to Error Message**
The overflow condition flows through:
1. Connection pool detection → `onPoolFailure(PoolFailureReason::Overflow)`
2. Router's upstream request handler converts → `Http::StreamResetReason::Overflow`
3. Router logs with `resetReasonToString()` → outputs "overflow"

The complete analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with file locations, symbols, and the call chain showing how the error propagates from detection to the logged message.

created, so the\\n58:   // stream must be anticipated.\\n59:   //\\n60:   // Also without this, we would never pre-establish a connection as the first\\n61:   // connection in a pool because pending/active streams could both be 0.\\n62:   int anticipated_streams = anticipate_incoming_stream ? 1 : 0;\\n63: \\n64:   // The number of streams we want to be provisioned for is the number plus the number of active streams.\\n68:   //\\n69:   // If preconnect ratio is not set, it defaults to 1, and this simplifies to the\\n70:   // legacy value of pending_streams_.size() >
